Chris Haynes of Yahoo Sports reports that Green even challenged his superstar teammate to leave. \u201cWe don\u2019t need you. We won without you,\u201d was the emotional forward\u2019s verbal gauntlet. Green and Durant were reunited on Thursday, and they appeared to have put the recent past behind them in the opening minutes. Things fell apart quickly after that, however, with the Warriors toppling to the Rockets 107-86 . Durant shot just 6 for 15, Green had as many turnovers as assists (five) and failed to score, and the Warriors simply looked shell-shocked.  It\u2019d be foolish to not mention the absence of two-time Kia MVP Stephen Curry (groin). It would also be equally silly to dismiss the remaining two-time Finals MVP (Durant), former Kia Defensive Player of the Year (Green), and a historically great 3-point shooter (Klay Thompson). It\u2019s too early in the season \u2014 and too soon after the Green-Durant tiff \u2014 to tell whether the Warriors\u2019 latest mini-drama will last. For Golden State, however, every day with their current dynastic makeup matters. Durant\u2019s free agency inches closer. The ripple effects from it will be very real and very expensive, one way or another. Will a November confrontation matter? Don\u2019t ask Durant. The Carmelo Anthony experiment came to a very abrupt end in Houston with the Rockets parting ways with the 10-time All-Star after just 13 games. Now they will rely on other means to replace the presence of Trevor Ariza and Luc Mbah a Moute, both of whom defected during the offseason. Night one of that adjustment went pretty well. The Rockets entered Thursday as a bottom-half team on defense. Then they held the Warriors to just 42.1 percent shooting, including a frigid 4-for-18 from 3-point range. Just as telling was who picked up the 30 nightly minutes that are now available with Anthony out of the picture. It\u2019s a one-night snapshot from a blowout win, but telling nuggets can still be found. Ennis and Clark are now Houston\u2019s best big wings not named PJ Tucker, and they\u2019re already being asked to shoulder a bigger load. Isaiah Hartenstein provided valuable stretch five minutes behind Capela and was a plus-27 in that playing time. On nights they don\u2019t produce, coach Mike D\u2019Antoni won\u2019t hesitate to bump his regulars\u2019 minutes back into the mid-30s. As for Anthony, don\u2019t assume that a win over the Warriors makes his odd departure any easier to witness for the stars who have shone alongside him. Speaking of stars having each other\u2019s backs\u2026 That\u2019s \u2744\ufe0f, Dwyane. At what point did DeMar DeRozan\u2019s brilliant, brilliant mind say, \u201cYeah, this the best and easiest way to score these two points right here\u201d? We need to see Chuck win one of these someday."},{"id":37421,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/lopez-twins-center-nba-evolution","date":"2018-11-16","title":"Lopez twins at center of NBA revolution","content":" Given their genealogy and shared background at Stanford, what\u2019s going on with Brook and Robin Lopez would seem to ripe for one of those scientific research studies on twins in some lab in Palo Alto, Calif. Short of that, it speaks to the divergent circumstances of their respective NBA teams, while offering up the veteran 7-foot centers as poster guys for the current challenges faced by the league\u2019s big men. On one side, you\u2019ve got Brook Lopez and the opportunities he and the Milwaukee Bucks have seized through the season\u2019s first four weeks. The Bucks have been bombing through their early schedule with one of the most unabashed 3-point-centric attacks , using their Lopez as a so-called stretch five. Head-scratchingly so, in fact, if you were to base his role on the first eight years he played in this league. On the other side, you\u2019ve got Robin Lopez, and the predicament he\u2019s in with the Chicago Bulls. The Bulls are down near the bottom of the Eastern Conference again, this time not by design (they played for lottery balls in 2017-18) but by the distress of multiple injuries. And yet their Lopez, though healthy, has been relegated to deep reserve and rah-rah status from the side as coach Fred Hoiberg and the team\u2019s front office focus on the team\u2019s younger players. Same age (30), same size, same position, same DNA. But with just enough variance in their skill sets and surroundings to yield almost diametrically opposed results. The brothers both will be in the house at Milwaukee\u2019s new Fiserv Forum Friday night ( 9:30 ET, ESPN ) for their 19th head-to-head meeting since they got to the NBA, five picks apart, in the 2008 Draft . But their current fortunes hardly could be more different. Right now, nurture is kicking nature\u2019s butt. The nickname crystallized on Twitter, courtesy of one @2LTDiesel, even as Milwaukee was still busy beating the Nuggets 121-114 Sunday in Denver. That\u2019s the game in which Brook Lopez essentially auditioned for a role in the Golden State Warriors\u2019 backcourt by hitting eight of his 13 3-point attempts, including 6-of-7 in the third quarter. Once on a roll, he seemed oblivious to the exact location of the 3-point line, needing to know only that he was behind it before he launched. At a time in league history when lumbering 7-footers represent little else besides obsolescence, Brook Lopez was going all Steph Curry or Klay Thompson on the Nuggets and on us. So there it was: One of the league\u2019s biggest players making like one of the Splash Brothers? \u201cSplash Mountain\u201d was born. Surely his brother and best friend Robin must have spoken to Brook and gotten some feel for his sibling\u2019s excitement. After all, they talk by phone daily. \u201cNo,\u201d Robin said 24 hours later, flatly, about asking Brook about the game he had. \u201cNot one time. It seems like they\u2019re doing pretty well. Looks like he\u2019s having fun out there.\u201d Fact is, while the brothers talk every day, they rarely discuss their jobs. They are a creative and curious pair, fans of comic books and cartoons (Robin had on a Chip \u2018N\u2019 Dale T-shirt before the Bulls game Monday, two characters from the Lopez\u2019s beloved Disney staple). They\u2019re intrigued by art, history, tech and hundreds of other topics, but claim to seldom, if ever, talk basketball. About the closest they come in regards to each other are some teasing jabs. Their publicly snarky relationship drew attention when Robin played for the Knicks in 2015-16, with Brook across the river in Brooklyn. Now they\u2019re geographically close again, 90 miles by way of I-94, Brook on a one-year deal with the Bucks while Robin is in the final year of his contract with Chicago. Sure enough, Robin had a dig for this occasion. \u201cYeah, yeah,\u201d he said of the Bucks\u2019 fit for his brother, \u201cthey\u2019ve figured out, what\u2019s best for him is, figuring out one thing he\u2019s really good at, limiting him, not giving him too much responsibility out there.\u201d Uh, not exactly. Milwaukee coach Mike Budenholzer has welcomed Lopez\u2019s size in recent clashes with the likes of Joel Embiid, Karl-Anthony Towns and Nikola Jokic. Neither of the Lopez brothers dazzles as a rebounder, but their fundamentals in attending to the boards historically boosts their teams\u2019 results in that category. Still, it is Lopez\u2019s ability to shoot from deep that has the Bucks revving so high. And this stretch five is a guy who made only three of 31 3-pointers (9.7 percent) in his first eight years combined.  So what gives? He made it sound like a skill lost but resurrected. \u201cA lot of players growing up can shoot the ball,\u201d Brook Lopez said. \u201cWhen you\u2019re just playing, scrimmaging or playing high school ball, you shoot it a little bit. But when I came into the league, I was really just a back-to-the-basket guy. There weren\u2019t many teams looking for a stretch-five then. \u201cSo it wasn\u2019t something I even thought about doing. I focused on getting my points in the paint. I still shot mid-range twos, but we never thought about pushing it past the three.\u201d That changed in the fall of 2016. Kenny Atkinson took over as head coach, bringing principles shared by his boss in Atlanta \u2013 the same Budenholzer for whom he nowplays. Encouraged to dust off that skill, Lopez launched 387 3-pointers for the Nets in 2016-17 and hit 134 (34.6 percent). That continued last season with the Lakers, where Lopez nearly matched his Brooklyn numbers. Now, green-lit with the Bucks and so far successful 41.8 percent of the time (41 of 98), he is on pace to shatter all 3-point marks for 7-footers. This is not unlike Clippers big man DeAndre Jordan unexpectedly cranking up his free-throw proficiency this season. Identifying it as a trend finally got Robin to chime in. \u201cWe\u2019ve all evolved as players throughout our tenure in the league,\u201d the Bulls big man said. \u201cThere have been times we recognize, \u2018I need to get better at this particular aspect of the game.\u2019 When someone like DeAndre or Brooks \u2026 recognizes, \u2018I want to work on this,\u2019 they know what it takes to get better at it.\u201d For the league\u2019s tallest, broadest players, with offenses focused on the fast and the far, there truly is a sense of adapt or perish. Brook is out in front of that \u2014 sometimes 26 feet out. \u201cI was playing inside and out in Brooklyn when I started shooting threes,\u201d he said. \u201cThen going to L.A., it was a big adjustment for me. My [playing] time went down, my usage went down. A lot of times I found myself just spacing the floor. \u201cIt was a whole new world for me. It was, \u2018OK, I\u2019ve got to find my shots from here now.\u2019 I wasn\u2019t finding my normal bunnies in the post or anything like that. \u2018I\u2019m just sitting and spacing \u2013 that\u2019s my job.\u2019 It was a big adjustment, getting the rhythm right and everything. \u201cI\u2019m pretty comfortable into that now and I\u2019ve kind of found my niche, as far as my rhythm.\u201d  Robin Lopez was penciled in as the Bulls\u2019 starting center this season. He was, after all, a highly paid ($14.3 million) veteran who had started all 450 games he had played since 2012-13. Chicago\u2019s other bigs were short on experience, raw in their skills or both: Bobby Portis, Cristiano Felicio, 2018 all-rookie Lauri Markkanen and newcomer Wendell Carter, Jr., the prized lottery pick for whom the Bulls steered themselves downward in the standings. Then everything got fast-tracked. Injuries to Markkanen and Portis, along with guards Kris Dunn and Denzel Valentine, have shifted Chicago\u2019s agenda. Carter\u2019s precociousness at both ends and off the court showed he could handle more minutes than anticipated. And Lopez\u2019s handling of the home stretch last spring, when he was a healthy scratch from 18 of the Bulls\u2019 final 26 games, had him facing the situation again. As helpful as Lopez was two years ago when the Bulls still were striving for the playoffs, as well as he played (10.4 ppg and 6.4 rpg), the bushy haired-and-scraggly bearded center fits neither the team\u2019s current timeline nor Hoiberg\u2019s preferred style of play. This Lopez is, er, a traditional NBA big \u2013 4-of-21 from the 3-point line over 11 seasons. \u201cHe\u2019s very talented and I think he can shoot the ball too,\u201d said brother Brook, who always has been the more offensive-adept twin (17.8 ppg vs. Robin\u2019s 8.9 in their careers). \u201cI\u2019ve seen it first-hand, growing up, playing with him my whole life. I know the value he adds to a team. \u201cObviously, the situation in Chicago, he\u2019s being professional. They\u2019re trying to play their young guys, and that\u2019s the way they want to go regardless of what happens on the court.\u201d Robin Lopez doesn\u2019t like it, mind you. He talked with the coaching staff about the diminished role and expectations. It generally is assumed Chicago would trade him if they could find a taker for his salary. But unlike last spring, when he sat on the side in street clothes, he is in uniform and available. Mostly he\u2019s called when one of the young guys picks up early fouls or if a particular substitution or matchup arises. \u201cI\u2019m a competitive person,\u201d Robin Lopez said. \u201cSo at first it was a change for me. But now, it\u2019s always just a pleasure to be in the arena. To be with the guys. To have some role on the team. Whatever I\u2019m doing, whether I\u2019m stepping on the floor or not.\u201d Said Carter, the quick-study rookie: \u201cIt\u2019s a great honor that he\u2019s allowing that to happen without too much pushback. He\u2019s being realistic. He knows what\u2019s going on. He\u2019s a great helper \u2013 he\u2019s not selfish at all. Behind close doors, he tells me where to be on defense, where to be on offense, how to be a great teammate. He wants to help me take over his role in a very good way.\u201d Or, as Lopez said recently about potentially getting cranky and refusing to help: \u201cI\u2019d be a huge jackass.\u201d Being as this is a Lopez, though, sibling deprecation is even better than self-deprecation. Asked if he was happy for his brother\u2019s re-invention in Milwaukee, for the step he has taken in his game and how Brook is getting some credit for the Bucks\u2019 strong start, Robin shrugged. \u201cSure.\u201d Brook responded in kind, verifying that \u2013 as much as their work situations change \u2013 the brothers\u2019 dynamic remains intact. Asked if he expected to bang against Robin Friday for the 19th time as NBA opponents (each man\u2019s team has won nine times), or perhaps wave to him from the court while Robin sits all night in warm-ups, Brook seized yet another opportunity. \u201cI\u2019m going to do my job regardless,\u201d Brook Lopez said. \u201cHonestly, I guess selfishly \u2013 but mean to Robin \u2013 I\u2019d rather he be out there so I could destroy him.\u201d * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. Rockets general manager Daryl Morey released a statement Thursday saying the team is \u201cparting ways\u201d with Anthony and \u201cworking toward a resolution.\u201d Anthony played just 10 games for Houston after signing a one-year, $2.4 million deal during the offseason. Morey added that: \u201cCarmelo had a tremendous approach during his time with the Rockets and accepted every role head coach Mike D\u2019Antoni gave him. The fit we envisioned when Carmelo chose to sign with the Rockets has not materialized, therefore we thought it was best to move on as any other outcome would have been unfair to him.\u201d Anthony was traded from the Oklahoma City Thunder to the Atlanta Hawks in July before the Hawks released him to clear the way for him to sign with the Rockets. Houston thought he could be the piece it needed to finally get past Golden State and win its first championship since back-to-back titles in 1994-95. Instead the Rockets limped out to a 6-7 start and the emergence of undrafted rookie Gary Clark made it appear that Anthony would have to take a reduced role. In the end the Rockets decided it would be better to move on than to force Anthony to do that. \u201cWe just had to see how things worked out,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said. \u201cAnd the way we play probably wasn\u2019t conducive to his game and he was trying to make the necessary sacrifices and it wasn\u2019t fair to him as a Hall of Fame player to play in a way that wasn\u2019t good for him, wasn\u2019t good for us. It just wasn\u2019t a fit.\u201d The 34-year-old Anthony is a 10-time All-Star who has had a tough time over the last two seasons. He averaged a career-low 16.2 points in 78 starts in a tumultuous season for the Thunder last season before coming to Houston \u2014 and accepting a reserve role for the first time in his 16-year career. Eight of Anthony\u2019s 10 appearances for the Rockets came off the bench after he had started all 1,054 games he\u2019d played in his first 15 NBA seasons. D\u2019Antoni said he feels for Anthony that things ended this way and made it clear that it wasn\u2019t a matter of Anthony not having the right attitude in Houston. \u201cIn the summer we tried to hit a home run and it didn\u2019t work out,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said. \u201cHe tried everything he could. He was great while he was here. It just didn\u2019t work out for whatever reason. I just thank him for his professionalism. It was good. He tried everything he could to make it work and it just didn\u2019t work out.\u201d The third overall pick in the 2003 draft has averaged 24 points, 6.5 rebounds and 3 assists in a career that also included stints with the Denver Nuggets and the New York Knicks. Anthony sat out Houston\u2019s last three games with what the team called an illness. His last appearance for Houston came in a blowout loss to Oklahoma City on Nov. 8 when he had two points and five rebounds. D\u2019Antoni expects the rest of the Rockets to handle this professionally, but knows that the move will be tough on them. \u201cI\u2019m sure they hate it,\u201d D\u2019Antoni said. \u201cThere\u2019s some good friends in there and there will be friendships. But above all this is a business.\u201d"},{"id":37397,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/nba-promotes-new-referees","date":"2018-11-15","title":"NBA promotes five referees to 2018-19 officiating staff","content":"NEW YORK \u2014 NBA G League referees Mousa Dagher, Ashley Moyer-Gleich, Matt Myers, Phenizee Ransom and Natalie Sago have been promoted to full-time NBA staff officials, it was announced today by Monty McCutchen, NBA  Vice President, Head of Referee Development and Training . The five officials join Brandon Adair as new additions to the full-time NBA officiating staff. Adair was added to the staff at the start of the 2018-19 season.  \u201cThese officials have excelled in the specific performance areas that warranted working NBA games on a regular basis,\u201d said McCutchen. \u201cAll five referees have achieved the pinnacle of their profession and will continue to work on their craft as they join the NBA officiating staff.\u201d In addition to their NBA assignments this season, the five new staff officials will continue to officiate NBA G League games. All NBA referees with fewer than four years of service in the NBA work NBA G League games to gain additional experience as Crew Chiefs and develop as leaders. New Full-Time NBA Staff Officials Mousa Dagher (Burbank, Calif.) is in his third season as an NBA G League referee. He officiated his first NBA regular-season game on Oct. 24. Dagher also has six years of collegiate officiating experience. A Syrian native, Dagher moved to the United States in 2006 at age 15. Ashley Moyer-Gleich  (Camp Hill, Pa.) is in her third season as an NBA G League referee, and she also officiated WNBA games in the 2018 season. She officiated her first NBA regular-season game on Oct. 22. Moyer-Gleich played basketball at Millersville University in Pennsylvania. Matt Myers (Jefferson City, Mo.) is in his 12th season as an NBA G League referee. He has officiated 15 NBA regular-season games. His experience also includes two seasons in the WNBA and 12 years in the collegiate ranks. Myers majored in Electrical Engineering at Hampton University in Virginia. Phenizee Ransom (East Point, Ga.) is in his seventh season as an NBA G League referee. His NBA G League assignments have included the Finals in 2017 and 2018. Ransom has officiated 13 NBA regular-season games. He played basketball at Winston-Salem State University and the University of Georgia. Natalie Sago (Farmington, Mo.) is in her fourth season as an NBA G League referee, and she has officiated three seasons in the WNBA. Sago officiated her first NBA regular-season game on Oct. 22. I\u2019m going to live with that because it works in my favor to the good \u2014 as my resume speaks and this team\u2019s resume speaks \u2014 moreso than it doesn\u2019t. Or \u2018Is it over?\u2019 Or \u2018did I force Kevin to leave?\u2019 \u2026 What you must know, nobody in this organization, from a player \u2014 not myself, not Kevin not anybody else \u2014 is going to beat us. Myers and coach Steve Kerr collaborated on the decision. Durant had not yet addressed the media Thursday, but he and Green were photographed on social media both entering shootaround together as well as shooting together on the same side of the court. In the closing seconds of regulation during Monday\u2019s 121-116 overtime loss on the road to the Clippers, Green secured a rebound and, with Durant calling for the ball, instead dribbled the length of the court into traffic and lost control as the Warriors failed to get a shot off. Durant was shown on camera visibly upset immediately afterward. Then, back on the bench waiting for the extra period to begin, the two traded words and gestured with Klay Thompson seated between them and Andre Iguodala, DeMarcus Cousins and others trying to calm the situation. Kerr said on Thursday he has faith that this disruption will not stop the Warriors from their bigger goals for the season. \u201cWe met in the locker room before practice and went through our usual gameday routine,\u201d Kerr said. \u201cWe addressed some things that will remain private. I know Kevin and Draymond have spoken. That\u2019s as much as I\u2019m going to reveal. I can tell you that I am extremely confident in this team\u2019s ability to get through any adversity. \u201cI know what this team is made of \u2026 I know the character of the group. I know the history of this group. It\u2019s way too strong and way too powerful to be upended by the type of adversity that may hit any team in the season.\u201d Green remained steadfast as well that this incident is not enough to shake the Warriors from their moorings. \u201cIf this only makes Kevin, myself and the rest of my teammates stronger, that\u2019s what it\u2019s going to do,\u201d Green said. \u201cYou think you saw something before, good luck with us now. We\u2019re not going to crumble off of an argument. We\u2019re going to move forward. That\u2019s all I\u2019ve got to say.\u201d For everyone who figures this franchise is perfect, Myers quickly cleared up that notion on Tuesday. \u201cIt\u2019s hard to win a championship. You can\u2019t allow anything else in your locker room, in the narrative. This team has done a good job of that,\u201d Myers said Tuesday. \u201cI know it may appear as if it\u2019s looked easy over the last however many years. It\u2019s not. If you\u2019re in our locker room, if you\u2019re in our organization, it\u2019s hard. The Warriors made the announcement of Green\u2019s suspension four hours before they were set to host Atlanta, and the 28-year-old Green served the suspension against the Hawks. Golden State won that game 110-103 , but Green was not at the arena for it. Jonas Jerebko started in place of Green and had season bests of 14 points and 14 rebounds. After the game, Durant\u2019s first public comments were more cranky than conciliatory. While minimizing the incident \u2014 \u201c(Expletive) happens in the NBA,\u201d he said \u2014 Durant didn\u2019t exactly bend over backwards to extend any olive branches. \u201cWhat happened, happened,\u201d he said. \u201cI don\u2019t really think that matters at this point (whether he and Green are friendly).\u201d Myers and Kerr have long supported Green\u2019s fiery nature that leads to technical fouls. Myers even sat with Green next door to Oracle Arena at the Oakland Coliseum when Green was suspended for a crucial Game 5 loss to LeBron James and the Cavaliers in the 2016 NBA Finals. The Warriors wound up losing in seven. These things happen sometimes over the course of an NBA season,\u201d Kerr said Tuesday. \u201cWe deal with it \u2014 again, internally \u2014 so any conversations that are happening or have happened it\u2019s our business.\u201d This wasn\u2019t the first verbal altercation between Durant, the two-time reigning NBA Finals MVP, and Green. In another overtime loss, 109-106 at Sacramento on Feb. 4, 2017, they shouted at each other and argued near the bench. Kerr said he spoke to Green, who was part of the recruiting group that worked to sway Durant to the Bay Area from Oklahoma City before the 2016-17 season. Green has been off to a strong start this season for the two-time defending NBA champions, averaging 7.5 points, 7.8 rebounds and 7.4 assists. Kerr has credited him for taking great care of the ball and establishing a tempo on both ends of the floor. The game at Los Angeles marked Green\u2019s return from a two-game absence with a sprained right foot and toe. James reached 31,420 career points with an and-one free throw in the fourth quarter to pass Chamberlain. James, 33, now sits directly behind Michael Jordan, Kobe Bryant, Karl Malone and Kareem Abdul-Jabbar on the NBA\u2019s all-time scoring list. James finished the game with a season-high 44 points, 10 rebounds and nine assists in the Lakers\u2019 126-117 win over the Portland Trail Blazers. His 44 points were the most a Laker has scored in a game since Kobe Bryant\u2019s 60-point performance in the final game of his career. The historic game ball and James\u2019 uniform will be donated to the I Promise School in Akron, LeBron announced after the game. After the game, James reflected on this history of the game, but wasn\u2019t about to reflect too much on what it meant to pass Chamberlain wearing a Lakers jersey. \u201cOne of the most dominant forces we ever had in our game along with Shaq,\u201d James said of Chamberlain. \u201cOne of the greatest Lakers ever to play the game. One hundred point scorer. One of the greatest scorers, rebounders to ever play this game. Multi-sport\/dimensional type of athlete. People had never seen something like that in that era. Then we give it an overall grade on a scale of 1-5 Robert Horrys, named for the patron saint of last-second answered prayers. Reggie Bullock hit a running lay-up off an inbounds play as time expired and the Pistons rallied from a 19-point deficit to beat the Raptors 106-104 , making a winner out of coach Dwane Casey in his return to Toronto. DIFFICULTY: Casey called timeout with 2 seconds left and designed a play with Jose Calderon lobbing a pass to Glenn Robinson III near the basket. But Pascal Siakam swatted the shot out of bounds along the baseline. Detroit took the ball under the basket with 1.2 seconds left, and Calderon inbounded to a cutting Bullock, who calmly hit the five-foot fadeaway for the win. GAME SITUATION: Kawhi Leonard tied the game at 104 with a jumper with 38 seconds remaining. Blake Griffin missed a jumper at the other end and Kyle Lowry grabbed the rebound, giving Toronto 10 seconds to try a go-ahead shot. Leonard brought the ball up but lost it out of bounds. CELEBRATION: Bullock was mobbed by ecstatic teammates, while Casey raised his arms in triumph, pumped his fist, then ran onto the court to celebrate with his new team on the court he once called home. GRADE: Considering the comeback and the buzz surrounding Casey\u2019s return to Toronto, it was a signature win for the Pistons, who had lost six straight games to the Raptors. Revenge is a dish best served at the buzzer. Four Horrys .  LeBron passes Chamberlain  With 44 points in the Lakers\u2019 126-117 victory over the Blazers, LeBron James moved past Wilt Chamberlain to become the fifth-leading scorer in NBA history. Fittingly, James passed Chamberlain with an old-fashioned three-point play . He drove in and hit a floater with 3:55 left in the game and got fouled. The ensuing free throw was James\u2019 39th point of the night and the 31,420th of his career. James\u2019 44 points was the most by any Laker since Kobe Bryant scored 60 in the final game of his career. Ahead of James on the NBA\u2019s career scoring list are Michael Jordan (32,292), Kobe Bryant (33,643), Karl Malone (36,928) and Kareem Abdul-Jabbar (38,387). Assuming James maintains his season scoring average (26.4 points) and doesn\u2019t miss more than a few games, he should pass Jordan before the All-Star break. Jimmy Butler had 14 points in his Philadelphia debut, but the 76ers surrendered a 16-point fourth-quarter lead and lost to the Magic 111-106 after Terrence Ross hit a tiebreaking 3-pointer with 8.7 seconds. Acquired Monday from Minnesota in a five-player trade, Butler played 33 minutes and shot 6-for-12 from the field. After the game, Butler talked about playing with new teammates, saying he has \u201cthe easy job:\u201d The four-time All-Star showed glimpses of why he was the headliner of the trade, but it was clear that it will take time to adjust to his new teammates. Butler generally deferred to his teammates on the court, especially to Joel Embiid, who posted his first career triple-double (19 points, 13 rebounds and 10 assists). \u2018Stache brothers reunion  The friendship between Steven Adams and Enes Kanter is a gift that keeps on giving. Fans roared in approval when a video tribute was shown during the first timeout. Players from both benches also stood and applauded as Casey acknowledged the crowd with a wave. Casey won 320 games in seven seasons with the Raptors, more than any other coach in franchise history. He was selected NBA Coach of the Year after Toronto set a team record with 59 wins last season, but had been fired by the time he received the award. Butler was greeted by more than 250 employees of the Philadelphia 76ers at his introductory news conference at the team\u2019s practice facility Tuesday. He made it clear winning a championship is his main priority. \u201cI already got enough money to have me and my family set for the rest of my life. They won 52 games last season and advanced to the Eastern Conference semifinals after going 75-253 combined the previous four years. Robert Covington, Dario Saric and Jerryd Bayless were traded to Minnesota along with a 2022 second-round draft pick for Butler and Justin Patton. \u201cWith Joel, Ben and Jimmy, we have a strong, dynamic team,\u201d Sixers general manager Elton Brand said, pointing to a \u201cchampionship window.\u201d Butler is expected to make his debut with his new team on Wednesday in Orlando ( 7 ET, NBA League Pass ). The deal to Philadelphia ends a two-month saga that began when Butler told the Timberwolves shortly before training camp that he wanted to be moved. Critics, often citing anonymous sources, called Butler a disruptive presence on a team. Nor do they expect the emotional Green to change after his one-game suspension by the team Tuesday. Green was suspended one game without pay for conduct detrimental to the team following an altercation a night earlier with Durant, though general manager Bob Myers declined to offer specifics on the All-Star forward\u2019s behavior that was considered going too far. Myers and Steve Kerr collaborated on the decision. \u201cWe just felt like this rose to the level of acting the way we did,\u201d Myers said, noting of Green: \u201cHe was professional. He loves to play basketball, which is all you can ask of him.\u201d The Warriors made the announcement about four hours before they were set to host Atlanta, and the 28-year-old Green was serving the suspension against the Hawks. He wasn\u2019t at Oracle Arena and didn\u2019t immediately respond to a text message seeking comment. \u201cI think we\u2019ll be fine,\u201d Kerr said. \u201cWe\u2019re a team that goes through stuff, just like everybody else. And things happen, bumps in the road. You\u2019ve got to move forward. It\u2019s all part of coaching a team, it\u2019s all part of being on a team. You have to get through the adversity and there are some difficult times and you just get through them.\u201d In the closing seconds of regulation during Monday\u2019s 121-116 overtime loss on the road to the Clippers, Green secured a rebound and, with Durant calling for the ball, instead dribbled the length of the court into traffic and lost control as the Warriors failed to get a shot off. Durant was shown on camera visibly upset immediately afterward. Then, back on the bench waiting for the extra period to begin, the two traded words and gestured with Klay Thompson seated between them and Andre Iguodala, DeMarcus Cousins and others trying to calm the situation. For everyone who figures this franchise is perfect, Myers quickly cleared up that notion. \u201cIt\u2019s hard to win a championship. You can\u2019t allow anything else in your locker room, in the narrative. This team has done a good job of that,\u201d Myers said. \u201cI know it may appear as if it\u2019s looked easy over the last however many years. It\u2019s not. If you\u2019re in our locker room, if you\u2019re in our organization, it\u2019s hard. \u201cAnd so they\u2019ll get through it, and we\u2019ll keep moving. Hopefully we get to the finals and win a championship. That\u2019s all anybody\u2019s thinking about, because I think that\u2019s all you can think about. Myers even sat with Green next door to Oracle Arena at the Oakland Coliseum when Green was suspended for a crucial Game 5 loss to LeBron James and the Cavaliers in the 2016 NBA Finals. The Warriors wound up losing in seven. Green apologized after yelling at Kerr during halftime of a game at Oklahoma City in February 2016. \u201cMy feeling on Draymond and his impact on our team doesn\u2019t change. (AP) \u2014 Jimmy Butler listens to country music, enjoys playing cards and drives a minivan. Oh, the four-time All-Star forward loves to win. Butler was greeted by more than 250 employees of the Philadelphia 76ers at his introductory news conference at the team\u2019s practice facility Tuesday. He made it clear winning a championship is his main priority. \u201cI already got enough money to have me and my family set for the rest of my life. It\u2019s not about the money,\u201d said Butler, who can opt out of his contract and become a free agent at the end of the season. \u201cI have to love where I\u2019m at and have a great chance to win a championship.\u201d The Sixers believe adding Butler to a roster that includes Joel Embiid and Ben Simmons will allow them to compete for an NBA title. They won 52 games last season and advanced to the Eastern Conference semifinals after going 75-253 combined the previous four years. Robert Covington, Dario Saric and Jerryd Bayless were traded to Minnesota along with a 2022 second-round draft pick for Butler and Justin Patton. \u201cWith Joel, Ben and Jimmy, we have a strong, dynamic team,\u201d Sixers general manager Elton Brand said, pointing to a \u201cchampionship window.\u201d Butler is expected to make his debut with his new team on Wednesday in Orlando ( 7 ET, NBA League Pass ). The 29-year-old Butler has averaged 21.8 points a game since the start of the 2014-15 season, the 13th-highest clip in the NBA over that span. The deal to Philadelphia ends a two-month saga that began when Butler told the Timberwolves shortly before training camp that he wanted to be moved. Critics, often citing anonymous sources, called Butler a disruptive presence on a team. Butler defended his reputation. \u201cYou really wouldn\u2019t know who I am unless you\u2019re around me every day,\u201d Butler said. \u201cFor the most part, that\u2019s why I don\u2019t worry too much about what everybody says. If you know me, if you\u2019re around me, you know my heart. You know how I go about what I go about. \u201cI love my teammates. I don\u2019t think there\u2019s too many of them that\u2019ll tell you that I\u2019m a bad teammate but people get whatever they want to say out. "},{"id":37491,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/jordan-enjoys-remarkable-turnaround-foul-line","date":"2018-11-13","title":"Mavs' Jordan enjoys astounding turnaround at free-throw line","content":" CHICAGO \u2013 There were times, Dallas Mavericks center DeAndre Jordan admits, when he would get fouled as he shot or attacked the rim and pray that the ball dropped through. Not for the points as much as to avoid embarrassment. \u201cAt times,\u201d Jordan said Monday of what understandably became an aversion to shooting free throws, \u201cI would try to make sure I made the [basket for an] \u2018and-one\u2019 so I would only have to shoot one free throw.\u201d The fewer the better for a player who shot a miserable 44.6 percent from the line over his first 10 seasons. Now, though, Jordan is cavorting through the league with the swagger of converting at 81.3 percent. That represents an 83 percent increase in his accuracy, this year over career. It\u2019s more of a breakthrough than an improvement, the sort of new trick old dogs aren\u2019t supposed to learn. But there it is: 39 of 48, Dallas\u2019 team leader in free throw percentage . \u201cI\u2019m not afraid of going there,\u201d Jordan said. \u201cYeah, I don\u2019t shy away from the line anymore.\u201d Nor should he. Jordan, through the Mavericks\u2019 first 13 games, looks to be cancelling his membership in the exclusive NBA club of elite big men who have struggled at the line. From Wilt Chamberlain in the 1960s and \u201870s to Shaquille O\u2019Neal, Tim Duncan and Dwight Howard, some of the most physically imposing players in league annals have been bedeviled when everything is still, no one is guarding them and the rim is staring back from 15 feet away. Generally, those giant talents were consistent in their misfires. O\u2019Neal, for instance, shot 52.7 percent from the line in his career and never better in a single season than 62.2. For Howard, the respective numbers are 56.6 and 67.1 . That level of reliable unreliability was what emboldened rival coaches to deploy their \u201chack-a-(take your pick),\u201d catch-up strategies, grinding games to a halt by intentionally sending deficient bigs to the line. Jordan\u2019s leap from 44.6 for his career to 81.3 in 2018-19 belongs to a special category. Not just mathematically but historically. \u201cA lot of people would never have believed it would be possible for him to make this kind of turnaround,\u201d Mavericks coach Rick Carlisle said. \u201cIt\u2019s one of the most amazing things I\u2019ve seen in the NBA in my 34 years.\u201d Said Chicago Bulls coach Fred Hoiberg: \u201cWe\u2019ve used that strategy in the past, but the way he\u2019s shooting the ball, he\u2019s one of the better free-throw shooters. It looks pretty good leaving his hand right now.\u201d Given how well Jordan has shot them this season, his 0-for-2 night against the Bulls Monday qualified as man-bites-dog news. And Dallas assistant Jamahl Mosley was quick to defend his team\u2019s center, saying he saw no backslide at all in Jordan\u2019s form. Mosley should know. He\u2019s the coach who spend the most time with Jordan in and after practices, and before games, grooving his lefthanded free-throw stroke through repetition and drills. Carlisle had a few suggestions for Jordan\u2019s mechanics over the summer and Dallas has a new shooting coach in Peter Patton. But interestingly, it\u2019s the club\u2019s defensive coordinator who has polished and sharpened this particular offensive threat.  Mosley, who worked with Denver and Cleveland before landing with the Mavs in 2014, had known Jordan for years. So when the free agent signed a one-year, $22.9 million deal in July, Mosley was the one who took him on as a pet project. \u201cThe way his form is, the way he shoots it, the way he structures it, the way Rick has talked to him about some things, I think it\u2019s the process of it,\u201d Mosley said. \u201cIt\u2019s literally focusing on that every single step. \u201cWe keep reiterating what we know he is: He\u2019s a good free throw shooter. In his mind and my mind and [Carlisle\u2019s] mind, he\u2019s a good free throw shooter. The more you reiterate that, the better vs. the other [negative] side of it.\u201d When the Mavericks\u2019 shootaround opened to the media Monday morning at United Center, Jordan was at the foul line on the arena\u2019s east end. He drained five in a row. Then he worked his way to the west end, waiting momentarily as backup center Salah Mejri \u2013 who made 58.4 percent (101 of 173) in his first three seasons but has yet to shoot a free throw this season \u2013 finished up. Jordan gave Mejri a smack on the rump as encouragement, then took his place. One make, one miss, one make \u2026 and then, as if synchronized to Jordan\u2019s fourth shot, a flurry of a half-dozen basketballs from various shooters crashed down on the rim at once, each blocking the next. Jordan looked peeved, holding his arms out in a \u201cWhat the (expletive)\u201d gesture. A maestro whose work was interrupted. He sank his next four. \u201cHe\u2019s always had a good touch,\u201d Mavs forward Dirk Nowitzki said. \u201cIt was never completely broke. I don\u2019t know, a lot of this league is confidence. I don\u2019t see anything different. He still keeps the ball really high. Now he\u2019s putting it all together. Maybe a change of scenery?\u201d Jordan is delighted to be in Dallas \u2014 three years after he accepted, waffled and bailed on the Mavericks in a free-agency dry run . And the Mavs feel the same about him. \u201cHe\u2019s a charismatic guy who\u2019s doing everything possible to try to bring our team together,\u201d Carlisle said. Jordan\u2019s presence in the paint and at the rim has cleaned up problems for Dallas near the basket. He is averaging 13.7 rebounds, while Dallas ranks fourth both in defensive rebound percentage (75.4) and fewest paint-points allowed (43.8). That makes his foul shooting a happy bonus. \u201cA lot of it\u2019s muscle memory,\u201d Jordan explained at the morning shootaround. Frequently, he as tried to avoid the topic in interviews, lest he jinx the work he\u2019s done or stop doing it. But he shared a bit Monday. \u201cI got a lot of reps up this summer,\u201d he said. \u201cI\u2019ve got a routine that I love and that I\u2019m comfortable with. But I also think it\u2019s mental because a guy can come out here and shoot 85, 90 percent in practice. But then in a game, it\u2019s a different situation, different pressure. To shoot that way, it confuses people.\u201d That\u2019s the legend of O\u2019Neal, who was said to excel from the line in an empty practice gym, then sputter when he the smelled popcorn on game night. \u201cRight. It\u2019s a different energy, man,\u201d Jordan said. \u201cIt\u2019s pressure \u2014 we all love that pressure, but it is a little pressure. It\u2019s fatigue. It\u2019s 20,000 people in the stands, too. So I think it\u2019s more so mental. You get into your own head about it.\u201d Jordan took a moment to defend the Diesel, by the way. \u201cShaq made \u2018em in clutch moments,\u201d he said. \u201cI guess, in clutch moments, your mind kind of locks back in and you fall back into your mechanics and the basics. But I know I got a lot of reps in this summer.\u201d  Curiously, Jordan\u2019s field-goal proficiency is at the other end of the spectrum. By virtue of ranking among the NBA\u2019s top three in dunks in each of the past eight seasons, his 67.2 career shooting percentage is the best in NBA history. (He led the league for five straight seasons, including three in a row above 70 percent.) Throwing down dunks, though, is different from draining free throws. Jordan seems to have his feet better aligned at the line, his left toe a few inches ahead of his right. He makes sure to release the ball high and drills for that in warm-ups, launching it almost straight up and only a few feet in front of him, just to focus on his arc. There\u2019s a little trigger mechanism he\u2019s been using, too, verbally checking his rebounders along the lane. Then he dribbles twice and only twice, before firing. \u201cWhere his percentage is right now, I think that\u2019s what he is,\u201d Mosley said. Then who was that guy from even one year ago? \u201cThat was more a case of looking at not the process but the end result,\u201d Mosley said. \u201cWhen you start to focus on the end result, good, bad or indifferent, you can start thinking, \u2018Oh, if I miss\u2026\u2019 Or \u2018If I make\u2026\u2019 versus doing the exact same thing, every single time.\u201d For Jordan \u2013 a one-time All-Star, two-time all-defense selection and three-time all-NBA pick at center \u2013 there\u2019s a new satisfaction to seeing the looks he gets now from opponents lined along the lane. \u201cHey, what\u2019s going on?\u201d more than a few have said to him, as his free throws swished. \u201cEverything takes time,\u201d Jordan said. \u201cWhich I\u2019m fine with. It\u2019s something where you never want to be content with or be complacent, you always want to get better.\u201d This hasn\u2019t been incremental, though, a mild dialing-up. This has been a bust-out. \u201cThat\u2019s the nature of the beast,\u201d Jordan said. \u201cYou want a breakthrough, but then you want to keep going. We\u2019re never satisfied with where we are as players.\u201d Hard to argue, since Jordan never has quite been here before. Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. If you have an issue with the rankings, or have a question or comment for John Schuhmann, send him an e-mail or contact him via Twitter . * * *"},{"id":37486,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/kyle-korver-qa-cavs-difficult-season","date":"2018-11-12","title":"Q&A: Sharpshooter Korver refocuses after Cavs' rough start to season","content":" Nobody puts Baby in the corner, but Kyle Korver heads there constantly and happily. That real estate \u2014 the extreme corners of courts throughout the NBA \u2014 is like Park Place and Boardwalk in this league, and Korver keeps his office there, with the best views and loftiest percentages. Korver\u2019s ability to space the floor from pretty much any point around the 3-point arc has made him one of the game\u2019s prized and best-known specialists. His accuracy from long distance, and often merely the threat of it, helped the teams on which he played \u2014 the Philadelphia 76ers, Utah Jazz, Chicago Bulls, Atlanta Hawks and now, Cleveland Cavaliers \u2014 reach the postseason 12 times in his 15 seasons. The No. 51 pick overall in 2003 , Korver was mostly a reserve in his first nine seasons. He became a starter in 2012 in Atlanta, however, and was an All-Star in 2014-15 with the Hawks. Korver\u2019s trade to the Cavaliers in January 2017 perked up the then-defending champs and got him to The Finals the past two years. And from 2009-10 to last season, Korver made 45 percent of his 3-pointers. This season? It\u2019s been different. His minutes are down (from 21.6 to 15.3), his 3-point percentage is down (38.7) and, of course, LeBron James is gone to the Los Angeles Lakers. The Cavaliers head into their home game Tuesday against Charlotte ( 7 p.m. ET, NBA TV ) with a 1-11 mark. They rank near the bottom statistically both offensively and defensively as they try to blend young players \u2014 notably, rookie point guard Collin Sexton \u2014 and veterans who have known better times into a new mix of styles and roles. That was just one of the topics Korver talked about with NBA.com\u2019s Steve Aschburner on Cleveland\u2019s weekend stop in Chicago:  * * * Steve Aschburner : As this season began, you said you were excited to be back. With so many changes even since then \u2014 injuries to Kevin Love and others, a coaching change from Tyronn Lue to Larry Drew after only six games \u2014 do you still feel that way? Kyle Korver : Yeah, I think you go into every season trying to be hopeful and optimistic. The part I was excited about, and still am excited about, is you\u2019re building a whole, brand new culture here. The last few years was kind of top-heavy with how we operated and how we played, and there has to be a new mindset. I like the building process \u2014 that\u2019s not the part that\u2019s hard. Losing\u2019s hard. And the injuries we\u2019ve had. It\u2019s hard to build the kind of culture you want when you\u2019re not healthy. It\u2019s hard to play. So we\u2019re losing. We\u2019re down bodies. There\u2019s been a coaching change. We\u2019re, what, [12] games in? A lot has happened.  SA : Quite a lot.  KK : We\u2019re all adjusting to going from the last few years to this new mindset. There\u2019s challenge to that, there\u2019s excitement to that and we\u2019re kind of caught in the middle trying to figure it all out. SA : Not to quibble, but what do you know about building a new culture? You\u2019ve been to the playoffs 12 times, including the past 11 years in a row. KK : Yeah, I haven\u2019t been on a lot of rebuilding teams, for sure. The only thing I can compare it to was when I went to Atlanta. Danny Ferry was the new GM and the whole \u201cAtlanta Hawks\u201d kind of got rebranded and rebuilt. they brought in coach [Mike Budenholzer], who brought in his staff, his philosophies and a ton of new players. I really liked those years. Building the culture \u2014 I enjoy that. But there\u2019s a lot that goes into that. You\u2019ve got to have a lot of pieces, not just on the team but throughout the organization. I think the Cavs are serious about that and working on it. SA : In training camp, Lue said you were \u201cin heaven\u201d in the revamped offense, given the movement and use of five men as opposed to the previous heavy reliance on isolation. Still heaven? KK : The last few games, we\u2019ve made progress in that. \u2026 The NBA, offensively and defensively, there\u2019s a shift in the league right now and we\u2019re trying to find our way. It\u2019s one thing to say, \u201cHere\u2019s our offense! This is how we\u2019re gonna play. Go out there and run it!\u201d But when you\u2019re going to make a lot of passes and a lot of cuts, and set a lot of screens and make a lot of reads, chemistry is a huge part of that. It\u2019s easy to draw up isolation basketball \u2014 it\u2019s not easy to draw up great motion offense with passing and cutting. There\u2019s a lot of feel to that and it takes time. We\u2019re at the beginning stages of it. SA : It would seem to allow less margin for error, with each pass or cut a potential turnover or mistake. KK : And we relied, the way we played the last few years, on LeBron to be the primary playmaker. So a lot of us have to kind of re-train our brain to be playmakers and not just get the ball and charge the basket or shoot right away. SA : Can you put into a few words, the Cavaliers with LeBron vs. the Cavaliers with LeBron?  KK : LeBron carries a certain weight. You feel him all the time. On the court, off the court, in the organization. I don\u2019t say weight in a bad way, but his presence is always felt. He is striving for greatness at all times. Because he\u2019s such a magnetic personality and such an incredible basketball player, people follow him. They look to him to lead the way. He was here for, how many years? So we have to create new leadership. Our own way. None of us is LeBron, on the court or off the court. There\u2019s an adjustment period for us all, to find our way, to find our voice. That takes time, because he filled all the gaps.  SA : LeBron is gone but Kevin Love [foot surgery] has been, too, for all practical purposes. It\u2019s probably not a coincidence that, last year, 66.3 percent of your shot attempts were considered \u201copen\u201d or \u201cwide open,\u201d according to NBA.com stats. This season so far? You\u2019re down to 48.9 percent. How much do you also miss the two-man game that you and Love honed last season, full of screens and passes? KK : [Sighs] I do miss it. Kevin is someone who, he and I had a nice little chemistry together. We could play off each other. Kevin is one of those guys where, a lot right now, the NBA is trying to switch everything and take away those threes, so you\u2019ve got to have guys who \u2014 if there is going to be a switch, you can punish it. Kevin is one of those guys. He can shoot outside, he can score inside. We had a nice little feel for each other in the playoffs there. So we miss Kevin in a lot of ways. SA : Already there have been trade rumors about some vets on this team, and they flared up again about you in particular with Jimmy Butler\u2019s trade to Philadelphia. The Sixers need shooting and that\u2019s where you began your career and still have deep roots. You\u2019re a player whose value rises as a season goes on. Are you prepared to play somewhere else? KK : You have to be. The NBA is a beautiful job in a lot of ways. But for living stability, thinking you\u2019re going to be somewhere for a long time, it\u2019s not for that. This is what you signed up for. You knew it going in, so you can\u2019t get mad about it. I have no idea what the future holds, to be honest. SA : This summer was different from previous ones. After another long playoff run and another loss in The Finals, you considered calling it quits. How did you make your decision to return? KK : That was a good four-to-six week process. I think after last year, my tank was just empty. If I can\u2019t put in the time to prepare in the offseason, I wouldn\u2019t feel good about just showing up and trying to \u201cjust hoop.\u201d I want to feel prepared, mentally and emotionally engaged with what I\u2019m doing. if I don\u2019t have those things, I\u2019m not going to be a very good player. And after everything that happened last year, with my family [Korver\u2019s youngest brother, Kirk, died unexpectedly in March ] and the playoffs and The Finals \u2026 I had to figure out first if my family was ready to do this again. It\u2019s not just about me.  SA : You\u2019ve got three little ones \u2014 Knox, Koen and Kyra \u2014 and your wife Juliet to consider. KK : My wife and I had to explore that \u2014 if we play another year, would we be OK in our marriage? Our kids are 6, 4 and 2, would they be OK? How many years are left? After giving it some time and letting the dust settle, and pulling yourself back up in the summertime, we were like, \u201cYeah, we\u2019re OK. We can keep going.\u201d SA : Had LeBron already made his decision to leave? KK : Oh yeah, he\u2019d already gone. My career\u2019s not based on LeBron. I like basketball. So it was like, \u201cDo you want to do this again?\u201d And I still love it. I went into the gym by myself \u2014 no rebounders, no friends, no family \u2014 and spent like two hours by myself thinking about it all. Dribbling and shooting. And I thought, \u201cI still love doing this, I really do. And my family\u2019s OK. Just keep going.\u201d SA : You\u2019re known for your offseason conditioning and a lot of varied, innovative workouts. But this sounds a lot more mental than physical. KK : It was definitely more that. My body, I\u2019m not too worried. But this is a big part of how I play \u2014 you have to be engaged 100 percent of the time. If I\u2019m not, I\u2019m not that good. SA : Has your family made sense yet of Kirk\u2019s death, which seized up on you all and was largely unexplained besides the shutting down of his internal organs? [Korver\u2019s parents, Kevin and Laine, had driven from their home in Iowa to the Cavs-Bulls game at United Center, and were joined by one brother and Korver\u2019s wife and kids.] KK : We haven\u2019t made sense of it. We didn\u2019t get a ton of answers. That\u2019s the hard thing. As we\u2019ve gone through this process, you hear story after story. So many people deal with this. Early death, and you\u2019re not sure why. It doesn\u2019t make it any easier, but it definitely it means there\u2019s this terrible club full of people that we can kind of lean on. But \u2026 yeah. SA : You rank fourth all time in 3-pointers made with 2,225 . At least, you do as we talk, because Steph Curry is 34 behind you. But among the top 25 on that all-time list, you and Rashard Lewis are the only ones who weren\u2019t first-round picks, and at No. 32 in 1998, he was drafted way earlier than you. Any special satisfaction from that?  KK : I\u2019ve purposely tried not to go down that path that much. I don\u2019t want to take away my focus. So I haven\u2019t given it any time. I try to see what\u2019s in front of me and keep on going forward, know that there are guys coming up quickly behind me [laughs]. SA : What do you remember about your first one? KK : I don\u2019t remember it. I do remember my first 3-point attempt . I missed it. In Philly, they had just come off the Larry Brown years [as coach] and they hadn\u2019t shot a lot of threes. I came in and shot one really quick, like in a few seconds. I missed it, but the whole place stood up and cheered. It was like, someone had come along to shoot some threes for them. SA : Any memorable threes?  KK : Some. The toughest one I ever hit, I don\u2019t even know if they have footage of it, it was so long ago. There were 24 seconds left in the game at New Orleans, and on an out-of-bounds play, I was running toward the corner when I caught it and shot it. Made it to force overtime. That\u2019s my memory, the hardest one I ever shot and made, and it tied the game at the buzzer.  SA : What do you consider to be the biggest change in NBA game since you\u2019ve been in the league? KK : It\u2019s the offensive freedom that guys are allowed to have. Obviously, players\u2019 skill sets have expanded with offensive philosophies. When I came in the league, you only shot a three if the ball went inside first \u2014 inside-out threes. The plays we had for threes, we only ran them if it was the end of the game and we needed a three. So it\u2019s really changed a lot, especially in the last five years. SA : How about changes off the court? KK : I think technology has changed everything. Everyone sees themselves as a business, as a brand. There are a lot more opportunities out there. How you conduct yourself, how you work \u2014 we don\u2019t really have offseasons anymore. Guys are constantly in the gym, constantly trying to get better, constantly improving their game. It\u2019s an all-year thing now. On the court, off the court. It\u2019s not just about playing in a nationally televised game. Everyone sees everything every night now. SA : Analytics, it would seem, has been a friend to you. Focusing on your specialty, the average team when you were a rookie took 1,224 3-pointers, taking about 18.7 percent of its shots from there. So far this season, coaches have shifted twice that portion of their attack to the arc \u2014 35.3 percent \u2014 and the average team will shoot nearly 2,500 threes. KK : For sure, for sure. It\u2019s been fun to have my career coincide with how the game has gone. To be a part of it in the beginning when things were just starting to change \u2014 my second year was when Steve Nash in Phoenix and [coach] Mike D\u2019Antoni really kind of came on \u2014 it was like, \u201cWhoa, this whole new style of basketball!\u201d And then it kind of became the norm. You saw different players come along and change the game \u2014 and change the way people see the game. What\u2019s a \u201cgood shot\u201d now is so different than back then. Then, it was \u201cHow do we get the ball in the paint? How do we get a good mid-range two?\u201d Now it\u2019s \u201cHow do you get a good corner three? How do you get shooters open? How do you space the floor better? How do you play faster?\u201d It\u2019s been fun to be a part of this whole \u2026 revolution, I guess? Evolution, revolution. SA : When you\u2019re in the car alone, are you music, talk radio or deep thoughts? KK : It depends. I\u2019ll do podcasts, a lot of spiritual things. I\u2019ll do music some times. Other times I like just quiet. Think and pray and get myself ready for the day. It\u2019s good to have \u2014 I need those 20 minutes, 30 minutes every day. So sometimes that car time is when I get my mind into it. SA : Last one. If you had NBA commissioner Adam Silver\u2019s job for one day, what would you do? KK : Hmm. I don\u2019t know. Our commissioner does a great job. I think he\u2019s on it. I\u2019d take his salary for a day, though. * * * Steve Aschburner has written about the NBA since 1980. On Nov. 12, 2010, Love made history with 31 points and 31 rebounds in a 112-103 Minnesota Timberwolves win against the New York Knicks. He set a team record with 31 rebounds, breaking the mark set by Al Jefferson on Jan. 13, 2010 , and became the first player with 30-plus points and 30-plus rebounds in a game since Moses Malone on Feb. 11, 1982 . Love grabbed 15 boards in the third quarter alone to will the Timberwolves to victory. \u201cIt seemed like no matter what anybody did I was going to go and get those rebounds. I don\u2019t know what to tell you,\u201d Love said sheepishly. \u201cI impressed myself. I don\u2019t even know what to say to be honest with you.\u201d Aside from joining the Hall of Famer Malone in elite company, he also joined another Hall of Famer in NBA lore with his game. Love\u2019s 30-30 game made him the first player with 30 or more rebounds in a game since Charles Barkley did so on Nov. 2, 1996. Overall, in the 2010-11 season, Love had 13 games where he recorded 20 or more rebounds and led the league in rebounds per game (15.2). "},{"id":37554,"link":"https:\/\/www.nba.com\/news\/jimmy-butlers-impact-sixers-stats-look","date":"2018-11-11","title":"Numbers to know: How Jimmy Butler will impact Sixers","content":" The Philadelphia 76ers are going all-in on winning now, having reportedly agreed to a trade that will send Robert Covington, Dario Saric, Jerryd Bayless and a 2022 second-round pick to Minnesota for disgruntled star Jimmy Butler and injured big man Justin Patton. The principles, of course, are Butler, Covington and Saric, with Philly dealing two starters for one. The Sixers now have a nominal \u201cBig Three\u201d in Butler, Ben Simmons and Joel Embiid. The question is how well they will fit together. Here are some numbers of note as we look at the new-look Sixers \u2026 The Sixers already have a primary ballhandler in Simmons. But when the game is on the line, Simmons takes a step backward. In each of the last two seasons, he has seen a drop in usage rate in clutch minutes, in part because he doesn\u2019t shoot from outside the paint and doesn\u2019t shoot well from the free throw line. Butler can obviously handle the ball more than Covington and Saric combined. He ranked sixth in the league in clutch usage rate last season, having used 41 percent of the Wolves\u2019 possessions while he was on the floor with the score within five in the last five minutes of the fourth quarter or overtime. Right now, the Sixers\u2019 go-to action on big possessions is a two-man game with Embiid and JJ Redick, which is difficult to defend in any situation. Embiid (18) and Redick (15) have taken 33 of the team\u2019s 47 shots in the clutch . A weak-side Butler\/Simmons pick-and-roll as a secondary option on those plays wouldn\u2019t be too bad. Non-clutch possessions are important, too. The Sixers are 8-5 after their overtime win over Charlotte on Friday, but they\u2019ve been outscored by seven points over their 13 games. They\u2019ve seen the league\u2019s sixth biggest drop in offensive efficiency, having scored 2.6 fewer points per 100 possessions than they did last season. Turnovers, as they\u2019ve always been, are an issue. The Sixers rank 25th in turnover rate , having coughed the ball up 15.6 times per 100 possessions. Shooting is another issue. The Sixers rank 21st in 3-point percentage (33.6 percent), down from 10th last season (36.9 percent). One big problem is that the Sixers are starting two guards \u2013 Simmons and Markelle Fultz \u2013 that can\u2019t shoot. The two former No. 1 picks have combined to make just 14 shots (on 61 attempts) from f rom outside the paint through 13 games, and the Sixers have scored just 94.2 points per 100 possessions (6.1 points per 100 possessions worse than the worst offense in the league) with the pair on the floor together. The Sixers\u2019 third point guard, T.J. McConnell, has attempted just two 3-pointers in 127 minutes. So three of the Sixers\u2019 top five guards are reluctant to shoot from deep. Saric\u2019s shooting has been bad, too. He was 13-for-56 (23 percent) from 3-point range before making eight of his 14 attempts over the last two games. Still, in regard to shooting, the Sixers gave up more than they got back in the trade. Covington and Saric led the team in catch-and-shoot 3-pointers last season, with Covington\u2019s 189 leading the entire league . Redick\u2019s shooting, combined with his relentless movement, is the more important complement to Simmons and Embiid, but having two forwards who can shoot off the catch has been critical. Butler (38.8 percent) has actually been a better catch-and-shoot 3-point shooter than both Covington (35.4 percent) and Saric (36.0 percent) over the last two-plus seasons, but not at the same volume, and he\u2019s been more likely to be inside the arc when shooting off the catch. On the other end of the floor, the Sixers just got smaller. They ranked third defensively last season and rank 10th this season , in part because they\u2019re huge, with four starters that are 6-9 (Covington), 6-10 (Saric), 6-10 (Simmons) and 7-0 (Embiid). Covington is now replaced by the 6-8 Butler. Simmons can surely defend the power forward position, the 6-9 Wilson Chandler is another versatile forward, and the 6-11 Mike Muscala will continue to play some minutes at the four next to Embiid. But the Sixers will lose some of their ability to consistently out-size their opponents. Butler is a terrific defender when engaged, but so is Covington, who led the league by a pretty comfortable margin in deflections per 36 minutes last season. In his final game with the Sixers, Covington was a big factor in keeping Kemba Walker in check until the fourth quarter on Friday. (In two games against the Sixers, Walker has shot 8-for-21 with Covington as his primary defender .) We can\u2019t assume that Sixers\u2019 roster won\u2019t change between now and March. They still have assets they can use to acquire more shooting. Last season, both Marco Belinelli and Ersan Ilyasova were signed after post-deadline buyouts and gave the team a big lift on the offensive end of the floor. * * * John Schuhmann is a senior stats analyst for NBA.com. Sometimes it\u2019s a transcendent individual season, one that doesn\u2019t need the assistance of a championship-caliber team effort to bolster the case ( see Russell Westbrook\u2019s win in 2017 ). Other times, it\u2019s a spectacular individual season combined with a best-in-show regular season from a team that inspires voters to cast their ballots for the player leading that charge ( see James Harden\u2019s romp to the finish line last season). And on those rare occasions when a otherworldly, all-time great individual season is paired with the greatest regular season in NBA history, you get a unicorn effort (see Stephen Curry\u2019s unanimous win in 2016 , when the Golden State Warriors finished 73-9). It\u2019s unclear right now just what type of season Giannis Antetokounmpo and the Milwaukee Bucks are in the midst of crafting. And they\u2019ve had a monster start in coach Mike Budenholzer\u2019s first season at the helm \u2026 but they\u2019re not necessarily on some record pace. What isn\u2019t up for debate, though, is Antetokounmpo\u2019s or the Bucks\u2019 readiness for prime time. They\u2019ve made that abundantly clear through the first 11 games of this season, serving notice that they are indeed prepared to take that next step. Budenholzer\u2019s reconstitution of the Bucks\u2019 collective DNA, with \u201cThe Greek Freak\u201d as the fuel cell for this revival, has the entire league on notice. And that includes the two-time defending champion Golden State Warriors, who allowed the second-most points of the Steve Kerr era in Thursday night\u2019s 134-111 rout at Oracle Arena. They pounded the Warriors inside, outscoring them 84-34 in the paint, and have shown themselves to be more than the one-man-band they played like far too often before Budenholzer showed up. \u201cI think teams are starting to take notice and realize we\u2019re not the Bucks that we were when I first got here six years ago,\u201d Bucks small forward Khris Middleton told ESPN after the game . \u201cWe\u2019re a totally different team even from last year.\u201d Antetokounmpo is certainly the same monster he was a season ago, only with another year of polish and a fresh set of directions from Budenholzer on how to attack the opposition and ultimately impose his will on the game each and every night. That\u2019s the main reason he\u2019s moved into the top spot of this week\u2019s Kia Race to the MVP Ladder. He\u2019s spent plenty of time on the list the past two seasons, but usually outside of the top five due to the Bucks\u2019 lack of team success. But with that shored up now with the new look provided by Budenholzer, the Greek Freak is free to sort through the different blueprints that could lead him to the finish line in this marathon. * * * The top five in the Week 1 edition of the 2018-19 Kia Race to the MVP Ladder: * * * Last week:  No. 3 Season stats:  25.6 points, 12.9 rebounds, 5.7 assists, 1.3 blocks Antetokounmpo is living up to his \u201cGreek Freak\u201d persona on a nightly basis, filling up the stats sheet and collecting jaw-dropping highlight plays at every turn. The difference this season is that his work is coming during a renaissance under first-year coach Mike Budenholzer, whose changes have worked wonders for both his best player and the roster at large. Look no further than the Bucks\u2019 (somewhat) surprising rout of the Golden State Warriors Thursday night at Oracle Arena. Antetokounmpo led the way with 24 points, nine rebounds, four assists, two blocks and two steals as the Bucks snapped the Warriors\u2019 eight-game win streak on a night that saw Warriors star Stephen Curry leave the game early with an adductor injury . It wasn\u2019t the Bucks\u2019 only statement win during this early stretch of the season but it was easily their biggest to date, sending a message to the rest of the league that what they\u2019ve seen so far from Antetokounmpo and his crew is very real. Last week:  No. 1 Season stats:  29.5 point, 6.1 assists, 5.0 rebounds That collective gasp you heard late Thursday night was Warriors Nation reacting to the announcement that Curry, after just 26 minutes , was done for the night after suffering a groin injury. An assortment of injuries are the only thing that has slowed Curry down in recent seasons. The Warriors have been able to manage without Curry in the past and will no doubt be able to do so this time around (if that\u2019s needed). But the two-time Kia MVP was off to a raucous start to this season and didn\u2019t need anything getting in the way of what had the makings of yet another monster MVP campaign. The Warriors certainly felt his absence down the stretch against the Bucks, who limited Curry to just 10 points on 5-for-14 shooting (0-for-4 on 3-pointers) before he exited the floor for the locker room. Meanwhile, the Warriors can only wait for word from the medical staff on Curry\u2019s situation. Last week:  No. 2 Season stats:  26.0 points, 8.0 rebounds, 3.3 assists If this NBA-best 11-1 start to the season has seen Leonard operating at half speed as he gets comfortable in coach Nick Nurse\u2019s system \u2014 as Leonard claimed after Wednesday\u2019s win against the Sacramento Kings \u2014 it\u2019s scary to think about just how good the Raptors will be when Leonard finally finds his groove. As it stands, Leonard has operated beautifully in the Raptors\u2019 engine this season and All-Star point guard Kyle Lowry is making an MVP case of his own. The Raptors\u2019 depth at every position has allowed them to maintain an elite level of play with or without Leonard on the floor so far this season. (Toronto easily handled the Los Angeles Lakers and Utah Jazz on their current road trip without Leonard in the mix because of a foot injury). He returned to the lineup in the win in Sacramento with an efficient 25 points, 11 rebounds and two assists. The true beauty of his fit with the Raptors is that he\u2019s been able to fit in seamlessly without even knowing the ins and outs of the system yet. Last week:  No. 5 Season stats:  26.6 points, 5.3 assists, 5.0 rebounds The Trail Blazers have won three straight games and six of their last seven riding the wave that Lillard and his backcourt mate, C.J. McCollum, have created with their attacking style early this season. The Blazers have done something that\u2019s often hard to do in this league: improve dramatically without an infusion of star talent. Much of what\u2019s working for them right now is the comfort that continuity provides. Without leaders like Lillard and McCollum, a youngster like Zach Collins might not be empowered to contribute the way he has in his second season. But with the tone being set in the offseason, there is no confusion about the roles every Blazer has. Lillard remains the true catalyst, the alpha if you will, and the man charged with finishing games the way he did Thursday night at Moda Center against the LA Clippers . That bench boost will come in handy when the Boston Celtics come to town Sunday night for a duel between two of the game\u2019s best finishers in Lillard and Kyrie Irving. Last week:  No. 4 Season stats:  24.4 points, 12.0 rebounds, 4.6 assists, 3.3 blocks Davis should be the easiest player in the league to evaluate on a game-by-game basis because of how the Pelicans\u2019 bottom line rests on him. And it\u2019s not his performance that dictates their fortunes, because he\u2019s operating at the highest level on the regular. It\u2019s his availability that is the true measure for the Pelicans. They lost six straight games after a 4-0 start to this season, a slide that coincided with an elbow sprain that cost Davis three games and sapped the entire group of much of that early energy. Davis turned in a 32-point, 15-rebound, four-block masterpiece in Wednesday\u2019s win over Chicago, snapping that losing streak and snapping out of an individual funk on the same night. Davis missed his first five shots against the Bulls before going on a tear and making eight straight to post his first 30-point game since Oct. 23. The Pelicans were desperate for a win in their first game back home after an ugly 0-5 road trip. If you subscribe to the theory that the true gauge for a player\u2019s value to his team is how they fare without him or when he\u2019s at something less than full strength, Davis has to be on any short list of the most valuable player candidates in this league. * * * 6.
